### Post by neuber on 2014-08-17

Using gparted would try to migrate HD space where the windows 8 pro to ubuntu 13 but the ext4 partition Linux does not appear in GParted. Tried using testdisk on linux as picture and when I click create the partition I want to "remount" also does not appear. Does anyone have solution for this case ??

### Post by gedakc on 2014-08-19
GParted uses the libparted library from the parted project.  To see if parted recognizes the partition, enter the following in a command window and look at the output.

> sudo parted /dev/sda unit s print

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-20
Better not to post screenshots of terminal output. Just copy & paste into post.
But if text is long, please use advanced Editor and add code tags or # in edit panel. Highlight text and click #.

If you still have the outside of disk issue:
[http://gparted.org/h2-fix-msdos-pt.php#partition-outside-disk](http://gparted.org/h2-fix-msdos-pt.php#partition-outside-disk)
Or see if testdisk will reset it, but sometimes testdisk creates the issue due to rounding between CHS and sectors.


Post these :
sudo parted -l
       sudo blkid -c /dev/null -o list

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-20
See if this shows error.

sudo fdisk -lu

And does this show details. This is also what you need to backup current partition table.
       First backup partition table, use your drive for sdX or sda, sdb etc.
sudo sfdisk -d /dev/sdX > parts_sda.txt

Post contents of parts_sda.txt

Then see if you can follow directions in the gparted.org link above.

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-20
Your extended partition is beyond the end of the drive.
sda4's end 625153409
drive end 625142448

That is often easier to fix than exporting the partition table and manually editing it and reimporting it with sfdisk.
Use fixparts and it should just update partition table with a write.

       Fixparts - Repair broken partition tables (not overlapping issues) & delete Stray gpt data from MBR drives
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1667614&p=10367957#post10367957](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1667614&p=10367957#post10367957)
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1705325](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1705325) 
[http://www.rodsbooks.com/fixparts/](http://www.rodsbooks.com/fixparts/)
First backup partition table, use your drive for sdX or sda, sdb etc.
sudo sfdisk -d /dev/sdX > parts.txt

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-21
If your drive is sda, use this otherwise change to correct drive:
sudo sfdisk -d /dev/sda > parts_sda.txt

And copy that file to another device. It is only if you have to go back for some reason.

When you remount or reboot you drive may change. Some users have flash drive become sda, and then hard drive is sdb. And on my system I skipped a port. My sde flash drive on reboot is sdb and all higher letter drives move up one. You do have to keep track.

Best to always check first, if not sure.
sudo fdisk -lu
or 
sudo parted -l

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-21
You cannot do anything until you fix the partition table.
Almost all tools stop working when they see corruption in partition table.

You need to backup partition table. 
Then use fixparts to rewrite a correct partition table.

After that then resizing partitions is another issue.

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-23
While I recommend gpt for any drive that will not ever have a BIOS install of Windows, if you have MBR(msdos) partitioning you cannot use gpt tools.

There are ways to convert a drive from gpt to MBR or MBR to gpt with only some risk of data loss. Of course good backups required and if booting Ubuntu you have to add a bios_grub partition for grub to install correctly. But that is a major change and with MBR partition table corruption is sure to cause even more issues.

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-23
All new drives start at 2048.

You will get warning messages. 
But drives have not used cylinders since hard drives went over 8MB back in the late 90's. So that is just an old warning that MBR still has since MBR is the very old partitioning system from the early 80's.

But you do not backup the partition like sda1, but the partition table on drive sda.

 Post the contents of this file, that you ran with the drive correctly:

[FONT=arial]sudo sfdisk -d /dev/sda > sda-backup.txt[/FONT]

---

### Post by LostFarmer on 2014-08-25
neuber- have never used fixparts but reading the tutorial all you need to do is run the program and then press 'w' for write partition table to disk, your problem will then be automatically corrected.  then run gparted and see if it is all good.

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-25
The issue was not sda1's size, if it was that would have corrected it.
It is that the extended partition sda4's end is beyond the end of the drive.

If your reloading the change to sda1 with sfdisk fixed the issue, it is because sfdisk also rewrote the end of the extended partition to be inside the end of the drive. Sometimes fdisk or sfdisk will do that.

If you still have issue then use fixparts. As it is the easiest way to get extended partition's length updated to be correct.

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-26
Drive end form above: [SIZE=1]6251[COLOR=#ff0000]42448[/COLOR] sectors
sda4 end from above: [SIZE=1]6251[COLOR=#ff0000]53409[/COLOR][/SIZE]
sda5 end from above: [SIZE=1]  625141743

[/SIZE]Only sda4 or the extended partition is larger than the end of the drive.
Use fixparts to rewrite partition table and it recalculates new end for the extended partition that will be inside the end of the drive. Since sda5 is already inside the end of the drive it has no issue.

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-26
I really suggest you read the instructions on the fixparts web site. I actually have never run it so I am just reading the directions to you.

[http://www.rodsbooks.com/fixparts/](http://www.rodsbooks.com/fixparts/)

You probably just have to do p to review partitions and a w to write the updates. q to quit, but that will not save changes which you need.

>  MBR command (? for help): ?
a       toggle the active/boot flag
c       recompute all CHS values
l       set partition as logical
o       omit partition
p       print the MBR partition table
q       quit without saving changes
r       set partition as primary
s       sort MBR partitions
t       change partition type code
w       write the MBR partition table to disk and exit

   MBR command (? for help):

[SIZE=1]The following instructions describe how to manually correct the problemof a partition extending beyond the end of the disk.

Other methods also exist, such asusing [testdisk]("http://www.cgsecurity.org/wiki/TestDisk")to scan the disk device to rebuild the partition table.  The testdiskapplication is included on [GParted Live]("http://gparted.org/livecd.php").

### Post by fantab on 2014-08-26
Running fixparts is as simple as:

```
sudo fixparts /dev/sda
```

Replace /dev/sda with the correct drive.

> FixParts checks the validity of the partitions it finds on your disk and will automatically (and silently) make adjustments for certain problems it finds. Thus, you may discover that your partition table is fine at this point. It's also possible that you'll see some changes in primary vs. logical status, or even omitted partitions...

 ...partition list includes no mention of extended partitions. If you don't know what this means, don't worry about it. If you do know what it means, you may want to know that FixParts discards the disk's extended partition as a matter of course and generates a new one when you save the partition table.

When you press '**?**' you will see the following:
```
MBR command (? for help): **?**

Press '**w**' to "write the MBR partition table to disk and exit". 
That is it. Fixparts has done its job.
a       toggle the active/boot flag
c       recompute all CHS values
l       set partition as logical
o       omit partition
p       print the MBR partition table
q       quit without saving changes
r       set partition as primary
s       sort MBR partitions
t       change partition type code
w       write the MBR partition table to disk and exit

MBR command (? for help):
```

Press '**w**' to "write the MBR partition table to disk and exit".
Thats it. Fixparts has done its job.

---

### Post by neuber on 2014-08-27
[SIZE=2][B][I][U]Can I transfer space of the windows partition (sda2) to linux partition (sda3) via Gparted ????

### Post by fantab on 2014-08-28
> **neuber said:**
> [SIZE=2][B][I][U]Can I transfer space of the windows partition (sda2) to linux partition (sda3) via Gparted ????

Is not dangerous delete partition sd4 ?? (I know how to delete sda4 using fixparts)[/U][/I][/B][/SIZE]

NO.

Always use Windows and Windows Partition tools to manage Windows.

Your /dev/sda4 is an Extended Partition and it contains Logical partition, SWAP /dev/sda5.
I suggest you delete this Extended Partition. Use Gparted. 
Delete /dev/sda5 first then /dev/sda4. Apply changes.
from the empty space create a new partition for SWAP. No real need to create an Extended partition again, just make it Primary and format as linux-swap.
Or you can use your earlier scheme with Extended Partition.

### Post by fantab on 2014-08-29
```
neuber@neuber-HP-EliteBook-8460p:~$ sudo parted -l
[sudo] password for neuber: 
Model: ATA ST320LT007-9ZV14 (scsi)
Disk /dev/sda: 320GB
Sector size (logical/physical): 512B/4096B
Partition Table: msdos

Number  Start   End    Size    Type     File system     Flags
 1      1049kB  368MB  367MB   primary  ntfs            boot
 2      368MB   292GB  292GB   primary  ntfs
 3      292GB   314GB  21,7GB  primary  ext4
 4      314GB   315GB  1363MB  primary  linux-swap(v1)
```

You cannot because of the swap partition above the space.
What you can do is delete the swap partition, then merge some of the 'space ' to /dev/sda3 and with remaining create new linux-SWAP partition.
Here is an old but relevant [Gparted tutorial]("http://www.dedoimedo.com/computers/gparted.html")... go through it...

Then you will have to edit the /etc/fstab file and replace the old Swap's UUID with the New SWAP's.
You can find the new UUID of the swap partition with the command:
```
sudo blkid
```...
... note down the UUID of your SWAP partition...

```
gksudo gedit /etc/fstab
```

replace the old UUID with the new one you noted down earlier. Save the file... exit.

Reboot and check...

---

### Post by fantab on 2014-08-29
Glad that its solved.
An observation: IMO you haven't given enough space for Ubuntu.
If you are not using a separate '/home' partition then have your '/' root partition atleast 50gb.
Having a separate /home is a good idea, in future if you need to re-install, I suggest you give more space to Ubuntu.
If I were you, I would install Ubuntu to HDD as following:
25-30Gb Ext4 Ubuntu '/'
2Gb Linux-SWAP
50-100Gb Ext4 Ubuntu '/home' partition.

To achieve the above partition scheme you will have to choose the 'Something Else' option during Ubuntu install from the 'Installation Type' step.
The above scheme is intended to keep the 'system' files and 'user' files separate.

regards...

---
